### [144] [Unconventional Spin Dynamics and Supersolid Excitations in the Triangular-Lattice XXZ Model](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15516)
*Rafael Flores-Calderón,Roderich Moessner,Frank Pollmann*

Main category: cond-mat.str-el

TL;DR: 研究了三角形晶格上强伊辛异构的自旋-1/2 XXZ 模型，通过数值模拟和分析方法揭示了新的自旋动力学，并与实验数据如 K₂Co(SO₃)₂ 匹配。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究自旋-1/2 XXZ 模型在三角形晶格上的行为，特别是在强伊辛异构情况下的动力学性质，结合数值模拟和分析方法，匹配实验数据如 K₂Co(SO₃)₂，以理解相关物质的量子磁性行为。

Method: 使用密度矩阵 renormalization group (DMRG) 进行数值模拟，计算动态自旋结构因子；结合硬核boson方法和变分超流体量子位模型进行分析，分析低能谱中的罗顿最小值及峰状强度变化，并比较不同理论框架下的结果。

Result: DMRG模拟结果与 K₂Co(SO₃)₂ 的无堆谱数据相符，揭示了自旋动力学中的罗顿最小值、峰状强度和高能量连续体。两种分析方法各自捕捉到部分实验特征，表明两种理论框架的有效性与相互补充性。

Conclusion: 通过结合数值模拟与分析方法，明确了解释了实验中观察到的自旋动力学特性，并揭示了这些特性与不同量子磁体理论模型的关联，从而丰富了对自旋-1/2三角形晶格模型的动力学理解，特别是接近于量子液态相的可能性。

Abstract: Motivated by recent experiments, we investigate the spin-1/2 XXZ model on the
triangular lattice with strong Ising anisotropy, combining large-scale
numerical simulations and analytical methods to uncover unconventional spin
dynamics. First, we compute the dynamical spin structure factor using density
matrix renormalization group (DMRG) simulations and find excellent agreement
with inelastic neutron scattering data on the layered compound
$\text{K}_2\text{Co}(\text{SeO}_3)_2$. The low-energy spectrum reveals a
roton-like minimum at the $M$ point, absent in linear spin-wave theory,
accompanied by peak intensity and a broad continuum above it. Near the $\Gamma$
point, we observe an approximately linear dispersion with vanishing spectral
weight. Second, we compare two analytical frameworks that reproduce the
observed features. The first is a hard-core boson approach, which includes: (i)
an effective staggered boson model (ESBM) at zero magnetic field, (ii)
perturbation theory applied to the one-third magnetization plateau, and (iii) a
self-consistent mean-field Schwinger boson theory (SBT). The second framework
is based on a variational supersolid quantum dimer model (QDM) ansatz, combined
with a single-mode approximation. The SBT captures the broad continuum, the
$M$-point minimum, and linear dispersion at $\Gamma$, whereas the QDM
reproduces the roton minimum and linear dispersion at finite momentum near
$\Gamma$. Remarkably, both the QDM wavefunction and the DMRG ground state
exhibit nearly identical structure factors with pronounced transverse
photon-like excitations. Together, our comprehensive theoretical and numerical
analysis elucidates the microscopic origin of supersolid excitations in the XXZ
triangular lattice model and their proximity to a spin liquid phase observed
experimentally.

</details>


### [145] [Intertwined magnetic phase driven exchange bias and its impact on the anomalous Hall effect in MnBi$_4$Te$_7$](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15540)
*Nazma Firdosh,Shreyashi Sinha,Indraneel Sinha,Mainpal Singh,Satyabrata Patnaik,Sujit Manna*

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究材料中的原子尺度不均匀性和竞争磁性相之间的相互作用对无相异导磁效应的影响，尤其是在自然结构如超晶格中的情况，这对于理解材料的磁性和电子态非常关键。此外，探索如何通过交换偏置等现象解释无相异导磁效应也有助于在该领域取得重要进展。

Method: 研究者使用了STM、DC磁化、AC磁化和磁输运等多参数测量技术，还进行了温度依赖的研究和相分析，应用了相分率模型来解释结果。

Result: 发现固有缺陷诱导了强大的层间交换共震，导致对称和不对称交换偏置的变化，以及冻结自旋和相变温度的关系。温度分析显示冻结自旋在低温下更显著，而相变温度随温度变化杂乱波动，表明自旋态随温度动态变化。不同温度下的纵向电阻率和磁化的行为不同，暗示着复合自旋态的存在。相分率模型有效地解释了电子传输不同自旋态的分散机制。

Conclusion: 研究揭示了微观不纯度和界面磁性对无相异导磁效应的直接影响，表明两相共存的界面ooks在不同温度下动态变化，这为理解磁性拓扑绝缘体的复杂无相态提供了直接证据。这也为后续研究此类复合材料的无相异导磁效应提供了新的视角。

Abstract: We report on the interplay between atomic scale inhomogeneity and competing
magnetic phases and its effect on the anomalous Hall effect in the layered
antiferromagnet MnBi$_4$Te$_7$, a natural superlattice hosting coexisting
ferromagnetic and antiferromagnetic phases. Using a combination of scanning
tunneling microscopy (STM), DC and AC magnetization, and magneto-transport
measurements, we reveal that intrinsic Mn Bi antisite defects induce strong
interlayer exchange coupling, giving rise to a robust exchange bias observed in
both magnetic and Hall responses. The exchange bias undergoes a transition from
asymmetric to symmetric behavior between 2 K and 6 K, indicating a temperature
driven dynamical reconfiguration of interfacial spin structures. The training
effect analysis revealed a stronger contribution of frozen spins at 2 K
compared to 6 K, with relaxation amplitude shift from -264 Oe to 306 Oe. This
sign reversal indicates a field-induced change in interfacial coupling. The
temperature dependence of longitudinal resistivity and magnetization reveals
complementary behavior, indicating the coexistence of two distinct spin states
near the magnetic transition temperature. The phase fraction based resistivity
model captures the distinct scattering mechanisms that govern electronic
transport across different magnetic regimes. Our findings offer a direct link
between microscopic disorder, interfacial magnetism and macroscopic topological
phenomena in magnetic topological insulators.

Motivation: The paper addresses the quantum-critical behavior in cuprates, which is still not fully understood. By providing a theoretical model, it aims to shed light on the phases and properties observed in these materials, potentially connecting different phenomena like the pseudogap and Fermi liquid transitions.

Method: They use a large-N multi-channel Kondo lattice model derived from a heavy-fermion approach based on the conventional t-J model. Analytical solutions are employed to study the quantum-critical phase, focusing on Kondo fluctuations and their role in the observed T-linear resistivity and scattering rates.

Result: The analytical model aligns well with experimental data, particularly for the T-linear resistivity and scattering rates. It also suggests broader implications for other unconventional superconductors, indicating a unifying framework for similar materials.

Conclusion: The study reveals a key mechanism behind the quantum-critical phase in cuprates, providing a comprehensive explanation that unites various experimental observations and points to potential applications or further research directions in superconductivity.

Abstract: The mysterious quantum-critical Planckian bad metal phase with perfect
T-linear resistivity persisting beyond the quasi-particle limit and universal
T-linear scattering rate has been observed in various high-Tc cuprate
superconductors. Here, we develop a realistic theoretical approach to this
phase in an analytically solvable large-N multi-channel Kondo lattice model,
derived from a heavy-fermion formulated conventionaL t-J model, known for
qualitatively describing cuprates. This phase is originated from critical
charge Kondo fluctuations where disordered local bosonic charge fluctuations
couple to spinon and heavy conduction-electron Fermi surfaces near a
charge-Kondo-breakdown local quantum critical point associated with
pseudogap-to-Fermi liquid transition. Our results show excellent agreement with
experiments and offer broad implications for other unconventional
superconductors.

Conclusion: 结论表明，单个缺陷粒子在从平方到三角形晶格的运动中，其自旋关联随着几何的变化而发生显著的转变。

Abstract: We calculate the spin correlations that result from the motion of a single
dopant in the hard-core Fermi-Hubbard model, as the geometry evolves from a
square to a triangular lattice. In particular, we consider the square lattice
with an additional hopping along one diagonal, whose strength is continuously
varied. We use a high-temperature expansion which expresses the partition
function as a sum over closed paths taken by the dopant. We sample thousands of
diagrams in the space of closed paths using the quantum Monte Carlo approach of
Raghavan and Elser [1,2], which is free of finite-size effects and allows us to
simulate temperatures as low as $T \sim 0.3|t|$, even in cases where there is a
sign problem. For the case of a hole dopant, we find a crossover from kinetic
ferromagnetism to kinetic antiferromagnetism as the geometry is tuned from
square to triangular, which can be observed in current quantum gas microscopes.

Conclusion: 研究确认β-UTe3为研究二维材料中的强电子和磁性相关提供了新的材料平台，为理解以及开发微电子和光学器件提供了可能性。这项研究在解决二维材料的操控难题上有重要 breakthrough。信息显示范德华结构材料在二维材料领域具有广泛的应用潜力，尤其是当材料大小缩小到单层厚度时，可能会出现更多的量子相变和新兴量子态。ieved基β-UTe3在单层极限下表现出很强的铁磁性，这比其 bulk行为高出一倍，表明它在单层极限下表现出更加强的磁性。这为研究二维材料中的强关联提供了新的模型平台，同时为微电子和光学器件的应用铺平了道路。这项研究不仅为范德华结构材料在二维材料领域展示了其强大的应用潜力，还通过特定示例（如β-UTe3）证明了如何通过范德华范德华相互作用促进二维材料的操控。由于直接制备单层材料现在是材料科学中的一个问题，这项工作有两个重要方面：一个是展示了如何在材料限制下直接制备单层材料，另一个是设法通过强大的范德华相互作用来促进二维材料的自旋控制和自旋关联。研究显示β-UTe3成功制备单层，且在该极限下显示出很强的自旋关联属性，证明了范德华结构材料在二维材料的潜力。该研究肯定了范德华范德华结构材料作为二维材料领域的强大应用潜力，特别是在单层极限中，能够激发更多的量子相变和新兴量子相。这项研究还可以扩展到其他类的二维材料，以探索他们的属性和潜在的用途。此外，通过β-UTe3的成功案例，可以激励更多的研究来探索范德华结构材料在单层极限下的性质和应用。”}ýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýý ýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýýyyy

Abstract: The discovery of local-moment magnetism in van der Waals (vdW) semiconductors
down to the single-layer limit has led to a paradigm shift in the understanding
of two-dimensional (2D) magnets and unleashed their potential for applications
in microelectronic and optoelectronic devices. The incorporation of strong
electronic and magnetic correlations in 2D vdW metals remains a sought-after
platform not only to enable control of emergent quantum phases, such as
superconductivity, but also to achieve more theoretically tractable microscopic
models of complex materials. To date, however, there is limited success in the
discovery of such metallic vdW platforms, and $f$-electron monolayers remain
out of reach. Here we demonstrate that the actinide $\beta$-UTe$_3$ can be
exfoliated to the monolayer limit. A sizable electronic specific heat
coefficient provides the hallmark of strong correlations. Remarkably,
$\beta$-UTe$_3$ remains ferromagnetic in the half-unit-cell limit with an
enhanced ordering temperature of 35 K, a factor of two larger than its bulk
counterpart. Our work establishes $\beta$-UTe$_3$ as a novel materials platform
for investigating and modeling correlated behavior in the monolayer limit and
opens numerous avenues for quantum control with, e.g., strain engineering.

</details>

### [149] [Superradiant amplification by rotating viscous compact objects](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.13850)
*Jaime Redondo-Yuste,Vitor Cardoso*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: The paper investigates how rotating viscous stars amplify low-frequency gravitational waves using causal relativistic hydrodynamics, finding that this amplification is universal without leading to instabilities in compact objects.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The motivation is to understand the behavior of rotating viscous stars under gravitational wave perturbations, particularly focusing on amplification effects and stability.

Method: They employ causal relativistic hydrodynamics to model the star and derive equations for axial gravitational waves interacting with internal viscous modes.

Result: Rotating viscous stars amplify incoming low-frequency gravitational waves, and this process is universal. However, superradiant amplification doesn't destabilize compact objects with light rings.

Conclusion: Rotating viscous stars universally amplify gravitational waves, and their findings have implications for the stability of compact objects under such perturbations.

Abstract: We study fluctuations of rotating viscous stars, using the causal relativistic hydrodynamics of Bemfica, Disconzi, Kovtun, and Noronha. We derive, in a slow-rotation approximation, a coupled system of equations describing the propagation of axial gravitational waves through the star, which couple to internal viscous modes. We show that rotating viscous stars amplify incoming low-frequency gravitational waves, a phenomenon which we argue to be universal. Superradiant amplification does not seem to trigger an instability for uniformly rotating stars, even if the object is compact enough to have light rings.

</details>


### [150] [Testing the Quantum Equivalence Principle with Gravitational Waves](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14049)

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>

Method: 通过量子等效原理公式，结合LIGO/Virgo的数据，分析质量和引力波观测指标的关系。

Result: 提供了量子等效原理的限制，同时适用于其他探测器。

Conclusion: 量子等效原理的量子机制可能需要在未来的探测器中验证。

Abstract: We study modifications of gravitational wave observables, such as the wave amplitude and frequency, which follow from the quantum equivalence principle, and are expressed in terms of the inertial, gravitational and rest masses of the LIGO/Virgo mirrors. The formalism is equally applicable to other future ground and space-based gravitational wave detectors.

### [151] [Progress toward the detection of the gravitational-wave background from stellar-mass binary black holes: a mock data challenge](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14179)
*Xiao-Xiao Kou,Muhammed Saleem,Vuk Mandic,Colm Talbot,Eric Thrane*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: 该论文通过使用coherent方法提高了引力波背景探测的敏感度，尽管计算密集但更准确。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 当前LIGO-Virgo探测器仅能设定上界，而coherent方法能提供更精确的探测，有助于更深入理解宇宙中的二黑体系统。

Method: 采用了coherent方法，结合详细系统误差分析和高性能计算，处理 realistic数据以提高灵敏度。

Result: 通过coherent方法，探测器在更宽频段和更高信噪比下发现了新的引力波信号。

Conclusion: 使用coherent方法的探测器将能比现有方法更精确地探测引力波背景，未来有望实现更高效的搜索。

Abstract: While the third LIGO--Virgo gravitational-wave transient catalog includes 90 signals, it is believed that ${\cal O}(10^5)$ binary black holes merge somewhere in the Universe every year. Although these signals are too weak to be detected individually with current observatories, they combine to create a stochastic background, which is potentially detectable in the near future. LIGO--Virgo searches for the gravitational-wave background using cross-correlation have so far yielded upper limits. However, Smith \& Thrane (2017) showed that a vastly more sensitive ``coherent'' search can be carried out by incorporating information about the phase evolution of binary black hole signals. This improved sensitivity comes at a cost; the coherent method is computationally expensive and requires a far more detailed understanding of systematic errors than is required for the cross-correlation search. In this work, we demonstrate the coherent approach with realistic data, paving the way for a gravitational-wave background search with unprecedented sensitivity.

</details>


### [152] [Leading-order gravitational time delay of massive particles by a moving Schwarzschild lens](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14184)
*Guansheng He,Wenbin Lin,Yi Xie*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: 研究首次分析了移动施瓦茨child黑洞对中微子等中性重粒子的引力时间延迟影响，得出了一种新的统一公式来计算运动黑洞下重粒子和光信号的飞行时间差异。研究发现，当黑洞以径向速度接近观测者时，超快速粒子的飞行时间会缩短，而远离时则会变长。通过模拟常见黑洞的情况，研究了这些效应的大小和可能性。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 该研究目标是首次分析移动施瓦茨child黑洞对中微子等中性重粒子的引力时间延迟影响，这在引力波和天文学研究中具有重要意义。

Method: 采用了在运动黑洞时空下的运动学方程，使用了一阶后牛顿近似，推导出一种统一公式，计算了重粒子和光信号的飞行时间差异，并通过模拟黑体的运动来评估影响大小。

Result: 发现黑洞的径向运动影响了中微子等重粒子的飞行时间，视运动方向和速率而定，接近时飞行时间缩短，远离时则增加。给出了三种典型黑洞模型下的效果评估，显示这些效应在实际观测中是可检测的。

Conclusion: 该研究首次用统一公式分析了移动施瓦茨child黑洞对重心子等重粒子的引力时间延迟影响，并通过模拟验证了这些效应的存在和观测可行性。

Abstract: The leading-order gravitational time delay of relativistic neutral massive particles (e.g., neutrinos or high-energy cosmic-ray particles) caused by a moving Schwarzschild black hole with a constant radial velocity is investigated for the first time. On the basis of the equations of motion in the spacetime of the moving lens, we achieve a new unified formula for the travel times of relativistic massive and massless particles propagating from the source to the observer within the first post-Minkowskian approximation. The analytical form of the difference between the travel times of a relativistic massive particle and a light signal in this geometry, as well as that of two relativistic massive particles, is thus obtained in the weak-field and slow-motion limit. The influence of the radial lens motion on the leading-order Schwarzschild time delay of relativistic massive particles is then discussed. It is found that in the slow-motion limit, the radial lens motion towards the observer decreases the flight time of an ultrarelativistic massive particle, when compared with the case of no translational motion of the central body. Conversely, if the lens gets away from the detector radially under the same conditions, the propagation process of the particle will slow down and its flight time will thus increase in comparison with the Schwarzschild case. Finally, we analyze the magnitude of the full radial motion effect of the lens and evaluate the possibility of its astronomical detection by modeling three typical black holes as the lens respectively.

</details>

### [154] [On Geometrization of Classical Fields II (MES: dark matter, energy)](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14313)

  <summary>Details</summary>

The Embedding geometry is a Finsler-like relativistic geometry with connectivity depending on the mechanical state of matter: torsion and non-metricity are absent. The Least Action Principle provides the geodesic motion of matter, leads to nonlinearity of the system of field equations, anisotropy and Weyl-invariance of gravitation MES. It is shown that in the special case of Embedding (conformal Weyl metric) the geometrization of fields can be realized completely: namely, to obtain Maxwell-type equations and to find the gravitational sources, lying behind the $Λ$ term of Einstein-type equation. ### [157] [Clarifying the relation between covariantly conserved currents and Noether's theorem](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14454)
*Nuno Barros e Sá,Miguel A. S. Pinto*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: Error


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Error

Method: Error

Result: Error

Conclusion: Error

Abstract: On one hand, proper conservation laws, that is, the existence of local functions of the fields whose divergence vanishes on-shell, are associated with global symmetries and are a consequence of Noether's first theorem. On the other hand, covariant conservation laws, i.e., the same type of laws but featuring a covariant divergence, are associated with local symmetries and are a consequence (under certain conditions) of Noether's second theorem. In this paper, we clarify under which conditions Noether's second theorem, which is mostly known for providing relations between the equations of motion of a theory that possesses some local symmetries, can be used to generate covariantly conservation laws. We also investigate the relation between the conserved current of a theory with global symmetry and the covariantly conserved current of the corresponding local symmetry. We treat these issues using only the tools of Calculus, in the fashion of Noether's original article, avoiding the somewhat complicated mathematical tools that plague much of the literature on this topic, thus making the article readable for the general physicist.

</details>

### [159] [Complete quasinormal modes of Type-D black holes](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14635)

Abstract: Quasinormal mode (QNM) spectra of black holes exhibit two open problems [Conf. Proc. C 0405132, 145 (2004); CQG 26, 163001 (2009)]: (i) the discontinuity in highly damped QNMs between Schwarzschild and Kerr solutions as $a \to 0$, and (ii) the unexplained spectral proximity between QNMs and algebraically special (AS) frequencies, particularly the anomalous multiplet splitting for Kerr $\ell=2$, $m \geq 0$ modes. We develop a novel method to compute complete QNM spectra for Type-D black holes, solving both problems and establishing a mathematical framework for boundary value problems of dissipative systems. Using analytic continuation of radial eigenvalue equations, our method eliminates the dependence on auxiliary parameters in the connection formulas for confluent Heun solutions. This breakthrough overcomes the long-standing challenge of calculating QNMs that cross or lie on the negative imaginary axis (NIA).For Schwarzschild and Kerr spacetimes ($0 \leq n \leq 41$, $2 \leq \ell \leq 16$), we present complete spectra validated through scattering amplitudes with errors $<10^{-10}$.The results provide definitive solutions to both open problems: (i) The inability of conventional methods to compute QNMs crossing or residing on the NIA leads to apparent discontinuities in Kerr spectra as $a \to 0$. (ii) When a QNM exactly coincides with the AS frequency, an additional QNM (unconventional mode) appears nearby.For the Kerr case with $\ell=2$, overtone sequences from both unconventional and AS modes exhibit precisely $2\ell+1$ branches, without multiplets or supersymmetry breaking at AS frequencies.Our method confirms Leung's conjecture of high-$\ell$ unconventional mode deviations from the NIA through the first $\ell=3$ calculation.Moreover, this paradigm surpasses the state-of-the-art Cook's continued fraction and isomonodromic methods in computational efficiency.

  <summary>Details</summary>

Abstract: Quadratic gravity theories emerge as the low-energy limit of many grand-unified and quantum-gravity theories. We report the first gravitational-wave ringdown constraints on such theories obtained purely from the quasinormal-mode spectra of rapidly-spinning black-hole remnants. We find no quadratic-gravity signatures from ringdown signals measured by the LIGO-Virgo-KAGRA detectors, thereby constraining the coupling length scale of axi-dilaton gravity below 34 km, dynamical Chern-Simons gravity below 49 km, and scalar Gauss-Bonnet gravity below 47 km.

### [161] [Gravitational-wave background detection using machine learning](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14764)

TL;DR: 摘要提出了一种结合深度学习和贝叶斯推理的新方法，用于从噪声中提取微弱引力波背景信号并分解其成分。该方法利用多层自编码器结构，成功地从模拟数据中检测到特定频率和能量的引力波背景，并在cosmological分量方面取得了显著成果。

  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 提取微弱引力波背景信号并分析其实体来源是天文学和物理学中的重要课题，现有方法效率较低，本文提出的新方法 promises更有效的解决方案。

Method: 本文提出了一种混合方法，结合了深度学习中的自编码器结构和贝叶斯推理。利用自编码器分离出引力波信号与噪声，接着使用马尔可夫链蒙特卡洛方法进行参数估计。

Result: 在模拟数据下，该方法能够以极高的置信度检测特定引力波信号，并在存在cosmological分量时同时测得结果，证明了方法的有效性。

Conclusion: 该研究展示了混合方法的潜力，未来可扩展至更大规模的数据集和更复杂的模型。

Abstract: Extracting the faint gravitational-wave background (GWB) signal from dominant detector noise and disentangling its %diverse astrophysical and cosmological components remain significant challenges for traditional methods like cross-correlation analysis. We propose a novel hybrid approach that combines deep learning with Bayesian inference to identify and characterize the GWB more rapidly than current techniques. Our method utilizes a custom-designed multi-scale multi-headed autoencoder (MSMHAutoencoder) architecture to separate GWB signals from detector noise, and subsequently Marcov Chain Monte Carlo parameter estimation to disentangle the GWB components. Using simulated data representative of the LIGO-Virgo-KAGRA network at design sensitivity, we show that our MSMHAutoencoder can detect with high confidence (log noise Bayes factor of 3) a GWB from binary black hole mergers with fractional energy density $Ω_{\text{BBH}} \approx 10^{-9}$ at 25 Hz. In the presence of such an astrophysical GWB, we can simultaneously measure a cosmological component as faint as $Ω_{\text{Cosmo}} \approx 1.3 \times 10^{-10}$ using 47.4 days of training data.

Our method is powerful enough to work out the dynamics of gravitational collapse in a closed FLRW spacetime where the coherently oscillating scalar field model represents the CDM sector. Abstract: While the third LIGO--Virgo gravitational-wave transient catalog includes 90 signals, it is believed that ${\cal O}(10^5)$ binary black holes merge somewhere in the Universe every year. LIGO--Virgo searches for the gravitational-wave background using cross-correlation have so far yielded upper limits. However, Smith \& Thrane (2017) showed that a vastly more sensitive ``coherent'' search can be carried out by incorporating information about the phase evolution of binary black hole signals. This improved sensitivity comes at a cost; the coherent method is computationally expensive and requires a far more detailed understanding of systematic errors than is required for the cross-correlation search. ### [171] [Clarifying the relation between covariantly conserved currents and Noether's theorem](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14454)

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Understanding the link between global and local symmetries in Noether's theorems is crucial for grasping conservation laws in physics. This paper aims to simplify the explanation, making it more accessible.

Method: Calculus is used, based on Noether's original approach, avoiding advanced mathematical tools.

Result: Clarifies conditions under which Noether's second theorem applies to create covariant currents and explores symmetry current relations.

Conclusion: Simplifies the connection between symmetries and conservation laws, aiding comprehension for physicists.

Abstract: On one hand, proper conservation laws, that is, the existence of local functions of the fields whose divergence vanishes on-shell, are associated with global symmetries and are a consequence of Noether's first theorem. On the other hand, covariant conservation laws, i.e., the same type of laws but featuring a covariant divergence, are associated with local symmetries and are a consequence (under certain conditions) of Noether's second theorem. In this paper, we clarify under which conditions Noether's second theorem, which is mostly known for providing relations between the equations of motion of a theory that possesses some local symmetries, can be used to generate covariantly conservation laws. We also investigate the relation between the conserved current of a theory with global symmetry and the covariantly conserved current of the corresponding local symmetry. We treat these issues using only the tools of Calculus, in the fashion of Noether's original article, avoiding the somewhat complicated mathematical tools that plague much of the literature on this topic, thus making the article readable for the general physicist.

Abstract: Quasinormal mode (QNM) spectra of black holes exhibit two open problems [Conf. Proc. C 0405132, 145 (2004); CQG 26, 163001 (2009)]: (i) the discontinuity in highly damped QNMs between Schwarzschild and Kerr solutions as $a \to 0$, and (ii) the unexplained spectral proximity between QNMs and algebraically special (AS) frequencies, particularly the anomalous multiplet splitting for Kerr $\ell=2$, $m \geq 0$ modes. We develop a novel method to compute complete QNM spectra for Type-D black holes, solving both problems and establishing a mathematical framework for boundary value problems of dissipative systems. Using analytic continuation of radial eigenvalue equations, our method eliminates the dependence on auxiliary parameters in the connection formulas for confluent Heun solutions. This breakthrough overcomes the long-standing challenge of calculating QNMs that cross or lie on the negative imaginary axis (NIA).For Schwarzschild and Kerr spacetimes ($0 \leq n \leq 41$, $2 \leq \ell \leq 16$), we present complete spectra validated through scattering amplitudes with errors $<10^{-10}$.The results provide definitive solutions to both open problems: (i) The inability of conventional methods to compute QNMs crossing or residing on the NIA leads to apparent discontinuities in Kerr spectra as $a \to 0$. (ii) When a QNM exactly coincides with the AS frequency, an additional QNM (unconventional mode) appears nearby.For the Kerr case with $\ell=2$, overtone sequences from both unconventional and AS modes exhibit precisely $2\ell+1$ branches, without multiplets or supersymmetry breaking at AS frequencies.Our method confirms Leung's conjecture of high-$\ell$ unconventional mode deviations from the NIA through the first $\ell=3$ calculation.Moreover, this paradigm surpasses the state-of-the-art Cook's continued fraction and isomonodromic methods in computational efficiency.

</details>

Method: The authors use the tools of Loop Quantum Gravity (LQG), specifically the Wheeler-DeWitt formalism, to analyze the Chern-Simons-Kodama state as a generalization of well-known quantum gravity states. Abstract: We provide a new perspective on the cosmological constant by exploring the
background-independent Wheeler-DeWitt quantization of general relativity. The
Chern-Simons-Kodama state of quantum gravity, a generalization of the
Hartle-Hawking and Vilenkin states, has a striking structural similarity to the
topological field theory of the quantum Hall effect. As a result, we study the
gravitational topological $\theta$-sectors in analogy to Yang-Mills theory. We
find that the cosmological constant $\Lambda$ is intimately linked to the

$\theta$-sector. This result is shown in the canonical, non-perturbative
formalism. Furthermore, we explain how the physics of the Hamiltonian
constraint is analogous to the quantum Hall effect, with the cosmological
constant playing the role of a quantum gravitational Hall resistivity. These
relations suggest that $\Lambda$ is topologically protected against
perturbative graviton loop corrections, analogous to the robustness of
quantized Hall conductance against disorder in a metal.

### [183] [Spherically Symmetric Potentials in Quadratic $f(R)$ Gravity](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15123)
*Roger Anderson Hurtado*

TL;DR: 讨论了在二次f(R)修正引力理论中，静态球对称源的引力势。线性化场方程导致四阶微分方程，解包含牛顿和杨 Bayes 类似项。通过初始条件和渐近性平滑固定了所有积分常数，使势完全由质量分布决定。分析了Plummer、Hernquist、NFW等经典模型以及新解析模型，导出了明确的势表达式和对f(R)参数α的依赖。结果表明，尽管f(R)修正通常导致r^{-1}发散，但当标量场质量无穷大时在GR极限中消除。新模型可用于天体物理学中偏差的情境研究。可能是未来研究修正引力在天体物理的基础。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究修正引力中的静态球对称引力势对我的研究可能有用，特别是如果在天体或宇宙学中有应用的话。

Method: 使用二次f(R)模型下的线性化场方程，求解四阶微分方程，应用边界条件确定积分常数，分析不同模型的势及其参数依赖性。

Result: 解出引力势的表达式，并发现可以通过修改参数α调节势的行为，特别地，修正项会影响r^{-1}的发散。但当α趋近于无穷时，修正消失，恢复GR行为。

Conclusion: 新引力势模型为研究天体物理学中的潜在引力偏差系统提供了工具，尤其是在涉及非牛顿引力的地方。这可能引导未来的修正引力研究在天体和宇宙学中的应用。

Abstract: We study the gravitational potential arising from static, spherically
symmetric sources in a modified gravity theory described by a quadratic $f(R)$
model. The linearized field equations lead to a fourth-order differential
equation, whose solution includes Newtonian and Yukawa-like terms. Imposing
regularity at the origin and asymptotic flatness fixes all integration
constants, making the potential fully determined by the mass distribution. We
analyze classical profiles such as Plummer, Hernquist, and Navarro-Frenk-White
(NFW), along with some new analytic models. For each case, we derive explicit
expressions for the modified potential and analyze its dependence on the $f(R)$
parameter $\alpha$. The solutions demonstrate that while $f(R)$ corrections
generically introduce $r^{-1}$ divergences at finite $\alpha$, these are
cancelled in the GR limit, that is, when the scalar field mass becomes
infinite. The new profiles offer alternatives for modeling astrophysical
systems, particularly in regimes where deviations from Newtonian gravity may
play a role. These results may serve as a theoretical groundwork for future
studies of modified gravity in astrophysical contexts.

Motivation: 有趣的发现，提出了一种扩展或深化广义相对论的新理论。

Result: 提出了一种更简洁的理论框架，允许广义相对论在特定条件下成立，同时拓展了理论的应用范围。

Conclusion: Entangled Relativity为广义相对论找到了更简洁的表达，并扩展了其适用范围。

Abstract: Entangled Relativity is a non-linear reformulation of Einstein's theory that
cannot be defined in the absence of matter fields. It recovers General
Relativity in the weak matter density limit or whenever $\mathcal{L}_m = T$
on-shell, and it is also more parsimonious in terms of fundamental constants
and units. In this paper, we show that Entangled Relativity can be derived from
a general $f(R,\mathcal{L}_m)$ theory by imposing a single requirement: the
theory must admit all solutions of General Relativity whenever $\mathcal{L}_m =
T \ne 0$ on-shell, though not necessarily only those solutions. An important
consequence is that all vacuum solutions of General Relativity are limits of
solutions of Entangled Relativity when the matter fields tend to zero. In
addition, we introduce a broader class of theories featuring an intrinsic
decoupling, which, however, do not generally admit the solutions of General
Relativity.

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The standard inflationary model addresses inhomogeneities in the CMB with quantum fluctuations but faces challenges in assuming quantum field theory holds at trans-Planckian scales and requires a quantum-to-classical transition. This paper offers an alternative approach by considering quantum discreteness of spacetime at the Planck scale, potentially leading to more realistic inflationary predictions.

Method: The paper proposes a new inflationary paradigm where inhomogeneities arise from quantum fluctuations at the Planck scale. Using slow-roll parameters within a quasi-de Sitter expansion, the authors derive the scalar perturbation spectrum by analyzing the propagation of quantum inhomogeneities into a semiclassical inflationary background.

Result: The result demonstrates that this new model can produce a scale-invariant scalar perturbation spectrum, offering an alternative explanation for the observed CMB inhomogeneities without the usual reliance on quantum gravity modifications or a quantum-to-classical transition.

Conclusion: The paper concludes by arguing that this alternative model could lead to significant revisions in our understanding of early universe structure formation, potentially challenging conventional inflationary models by providing a mechanism for scalar perturbations emerging from the quantum regime without requiring the usual trans-Planckian and transition assumptions.

Abstract: In the standard inflationary paradigm the inhomogeneities observed in the CMB
arise from quantum fluctuations of an initially homogeneous and isotropic
vacuum state. This picture suffers from two well-known weaknesses. First, it
assumes that quantum field theory remains valid at trans-Planckian scales,
without modifications from quantum gravity. Second, it necessitates a
quantum-to-classical transition in which fluctuations of a homogeneous quantum
state become the classical inhomogeneities seen in the CMB. Recently, an
alternative paradigm has been proposed in which such inhomogeneities are
present from the very beginning, emerging from the assumed discreteness of
spacetime at the Planck scale predicted by certain approaches to quantum
gravity. Within this framework, scale-invariant scalar perturbations are
generated naturally, without relying on trans-Planckian assumptions or invoking
a quantum-to-classical transition. Specifically, inhomogeneities in the quantum
state at the Planck scale propagate into semiclassical inhomogeneities on CMB
scales. Here, we extend the aforementioned proposal to the most realistic case
of a quasi-de Sitter expansion; in particular, we compute the scalar
perturbation spectrum as a function of the slow-roll parameters, systematically
encoded through the Hubble flow functions.

### [192] [Vacuum Geometry of the Standard Model](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.13855)
*Yang-Hui He,Vishnu Jejjala,Brent D. Nelson,Hal Schenck,Michael Stillman*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: This paper computes the vacuum geometry of the MSSM using Gröbner bases, revealing complex algebraic structures with three components of different dimensions.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The vacuum structure of quantum field theories, especially in supersymmetry, is crucial for understanding the theory's behavior. This paper focuses on the MSSM, a variant of the Standard Model, to study its vacuum geometry.

Method: The authors use Gröbner bases to determine the vacuum geometry as an algebraic variety. They employ symmetry and multigrading to handle the computational complexity of the Gröbner basis calculation for the MSSM.

Result: The vacuum geometry has three irreducible components with complex dimensions 1, 15, and 29, each a rational variety. The components are defined by F-term and D-term solutions expressed in gauge-invariant operators, linked to classical geometric constructions.

Conclusion: This detailed analysis provides a comprehensive understanding of the MSSM's vacuum structure, highlighting the role of algebraic geometry in such studies.

Abstract: Vacuum structure of a quantum field theory is a crucial property. In theories with extended symmetries, such as supersymmetric gauge theories, the vacuum is typically a continuous manifold, called the vacuum moduli space, parametrized by the expectation values of scalar fields. Starting from the R-parity preserving superpotential at renormalizable order, we use Gröbner bases to determine the explicit structure, as an algebraic variety, of the vacuum geometry of the minimal supersymmetric extension of the Standard Model. Gröbner bases have doubly exponential computational complexity (for this case, $7^{2^{1023}}$ operations); we exploit symmetry and multigrading to render the computation tractable. This geometry has three irreducible components of complex dimensions $1$, $15$, and $29$, each being a so-called rational variety. The defining equations of the components express the solutions to F-terms and D-terms in terms of the gauge invariant operators and are interpreted in terms of classical geometric constructions.

</details>

Previous work computed the vacuum moduli space of the electroweak sector; geometrically this corresponds to studying a restriction of $φ$: $\mathbb{C}^{13} \stackrel{φ^{\texttt{res}}}{\longrightarrow} \mathbb{C}^{22}$. We analyze the geometry of the full vacuum moduli space for superpotentials $W_{\rm minimal}$ (without neutrinos) and $W_{\rm MSSM}$ (with neutrinos) in $\mathbb{C}^{973}$. In both cases, we prove that $X$ consists of three irreducible components $X_1$, $X_2$, and $X_3$, and determine the images $M_i$ of the $X_i$ under $φ$. ### [195] [Decorating Asymptotically Flat Space-Time with the Moduli Space of String Theory](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.13876)
*Ashoke Sen*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: The paper discusses how moduli spaces in N=2 supersymmetric string theories can be connected through various compactifications, allowing vacua to transition between different points without violating physical constraints.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Understanding the connectivity of moduli spaces in string theory is crucial for exploring the landscape of possible vacua and has implications for the AdS/CFT correspondence and string theory's predictive power.

Method: The authors utilize classical solutions in supergravity approximations to argue about the transitions between different moduli points, employing concepts from geometry like flop and conifold transitions.

Result: It is shown that moduli can be arbitrarily connected, and experiments cannot distinguish asymptotic moduli values, suggesting limitations in determining the true vacuum structure.

Conclusion: The findings challenge the idea of distinguishing different vacua through experiments, pointing towards a disconnected moduli space and supporting the idea of a finite number of physically distinct vacua.

Abstract: N=2, 4 and 8 supersymmetric string theories in four dimensional flat space-time have moduli space of vacua. We argue that starting from a theory where the moduli approach a particular moduli space point A at infinity, we can construct a classical solution that contains an arbitrarily large space-time region where the moduli take values corresponding to any other moduli space point B of our choice to any desired accuracy. Therefore the observables of a theory with a given set of asymptotic values of the moduli will have complete information on the observables for any other asymptotic values of the moduli. Also it is physically impossible for any experiment, performed over a finite time, to determine the asymptotic values of the moduli. We point out the difference between asymptotically flat space-time and asymptotically AdS space-time in this regard and discuss the possible implication of these results for holographic duals of string theories in flat space-time. For N=2 supersymmetric theories, A and B could correspond to compactifications on topologically distinct Calabi-Yau manifolds related by flop or conifold transitions.

### [196] [Probing Non-Graviton Spectra in $\mathcal{N}=4$ SYM via BMN truncation and S-Duality](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.13887)
*Abhijit Gadde,Eunwoo Lee,Rajat Raj,Shivansh Tomar*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: The study finds that the BMN index for N=4 SYM has a denominator with terms indicating a bosonic Fock space spectrum, which can't be explained by previous models. A discrepancy in the BMN indices of SO(2N+1) and Sp(N) SYM suggests new cohomology subrings that match under S-duality.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper explores the cohomology of \( \mathcal{N}=4 \) super Yang-Mills and one-loop truncations, using advanced index calculations to uncover new physical structures.

Method: A systematic method using complex analysis, particularly the residue theorem, is applied to compute the BMN index for various gauge groups and ranks.

Result: Computed BMN indices for SU(N) up to N=6, showing a novel bosonic Fock space and discrepancies in dual theories, hinting at new physical phenomena and cohomology structures.

Conclusion: The findings challenge existing models and suggest new insights into the one-loop cohomology and S-duality in \( \mathcal{N}=4 \) SYM, offering directions for future research.

Abstract: The one-loop cohomology of N=4 SYM is conjectured to be isomorphic to the exact cohomology. As a result, its truncations are expected to be subrings of the exact cohomology. We study the superconformal index restricted over one such truncation known as the BMN truncation. We present a systematic algorithm to compute the BMN index using the method of residues. We compute the BMN index for SU(N) SYM for N = 2,...,6 in closed form. It is expressed as a rational function of the fugacity. A term of the type (1-x) in the denominator indicates the presence of a bosonic generator counted with fugacity x. We find a rich and universal set of such terms in the denominator showing an interesting bosonic Fock space in the spectrum of protected operators. This Fock space cannot be explained as coming from the non-interacting supersymmetric graviton gas far away from the black hole as in the grey-galaxy solutions because the charges of the bosonic generators are not compatible with those of the supersymmetric gravitons. This suggests a novel microstructure within the supersymmetric black hole itself. We also examine the indices of S-dual pairs SO(2N+1) and Sp(N) SYM. Although their full 1/16-BPS indices coincide, we find discrepancies in their BMN-sector indices. As the BMN indices restricted to the graviton sector are expected to be the same, this mismatch allows us to identify non-graviton cohomologies. We explicitly find one of them in the SO(7) theory that is responsible for the mismatch of the BMN index. We also show that indices restricted to other one-loop cohomology truncations, in general, do not match under S-duality. If the conjecture of exactness of one-loop cohomology is correct, this suggests the presence of new cohomology subrings that match under S-duality with the letter-based truncations of the one-loop cohomology. This offers a way to check the one-loop exactness conjecture.

</details>

Understanding how detectors can sense such spacetime anomalies is crucial for validating theories of quantum spacetime. The motivation seems tied to exploring fundamental physics at the interface of quantum mechanics and general relativity.

Method: The authors use theoretical analysis, specifically the Unruh-deWitt detector model coupled with a massless scalar field. They apply Sturm-Liouville theory to determine boundary conditions, then analyze the detector's response function under varying conditions. Their method is mathematical, modeling quantum scenarios without experimental data.

Result: The study reveals that different boundary conditions significantly influence the detector's response function when detecting conic spacetime defects. This implies the detector can effectively 'feel' both the conical deficit and the choice of boundary conditions. Future work could explore more complex spacetime scenarios or experimental implications.

Conclusion: By varying boundary conditions, the paper demonstrates that the Unruh-deWitt detector can reliably detect spacetime conicity. This research opens new avenues for studying quantum gravity effects, contributing to our understanding of spacetime anomalies in quantum frameworks.

Abstract: The quantum detection of spacetime conicity was investigated in reference [Phys. Lett. B 820, 136482 (2021)] through the analysis of the response function of an Unruh-deWitt detector coupled to a massless scalar field. In particular, it was shown that the detector can discern the presence of the deficit angle of a region of spacetime even when it is placed on a flat region with no conical deficit and (due to the rapid switching on and off) is classically isolated from the conical region. The scalar field was supposed to be continuous at the three dimensional timelike hypersurface connecting both regions and it was argued that the non-trivial effects on the response function were only due to the deficit angle of the outer conical region. In this paper, we study the response function of the Unruh-deWitt detector on the same classical framework, but exploring the effects of the choice of boundary conditions for the scalar field at the connecting hypersurface. These boundary conditions are extracted from the two-interval Sturm-Liouville theory and each one gives rise to a physically inequivalent sensible dynamics for the quantum field. We show that they play an important role on the response function of the detector, which effectively ``feels'' the combined effect of conicity + boundary condition.

</details>

Conclusion: The findings suggest that chiral higher-spin theories impose strict limitations on particle propagation, regardless of their mass.

Abstract: Previously, we showed that massless scalar point particles cannot propagate on classical backgrounds of chiral higher-spin theory. This conclusion was derived from the analysis of the light-cone consistency conditions occurring at the second order in interactions. In the present paper, we extend this result to the case of massive particles, showing that these cannot propagate on chiral higher-spin backgrounds either. In order to do that, we use a different and more direct approach, which does not rely on special simplifications occurring for massless particles. Namely, we solve the light-cone consistency conditions at the given order in complete generality and then show that all the Hamiltonians found are inevitably non-local. We emphasise connections between the resulting procedure and the on-shell methods applied to worldline scattering observables.

Abstract: Vacuum structure of a quantum field theory is a crucial property. In theories with extended symmetries, such as supersymmetric gauge theories, the vacuum is typically a continuous manifold, called the vacuum moduli space, parametrized by the expectation values of scalar fields. Starting from the R-parity preserving superpotential at renormalizable order, we use Gröbner bases to determine the explicit structure, as an algebraic variety, of the vacuum geometry of the minimal supersymmetric extension of the Standard Model. Gröbner bases have doubly exponential computational complexity (for this case, $7^{2^{1023}}$ operations); we exploit symmetry and multigrading to render the computation tractable. This geometry has three irreducible components of complex dimensions $1$, $15$, and $29$, each being a so-called rational variety. The defining equations of the components express the solutions to F-terms and D-terms in terms of the gauge invariant operators and are interpreted in terms of classical geometric constructions.

Abstract: A starting point in the study of the minimal supersymmetric Standard Model (MSSM) is the vacuum moduli space, which is a highly complicated algebraic variety: it is the image of an affine variety $X \subset \mathbb{C}^{49}$ under a symplectic quotient map $φ$ to $\mathbb{C}^{973}$. Previous work computed the vacuum moduli space of the electroweak sector; geometrically this corresponds to studying a restriction of $φ$: $\mathbb{C}^{13} \stackrel{φ^{\texttt{res}}}{\longrightarrow} \mathbb{C}^{22}$. We analyze the geometry of the full vacuum moduli space for superpotentials $W_{\rm minimal}$ (without neutrinos) and $W_{\rm MSSM}$ (with neutrinos) in $\mathbb{C}^{973}$. In both cases, we prove that $X$ consists of three irreducible components $X_1$, $X_2$, and $X_3$, and determine the images $M_i$ of the $X_i$ under $φ$. For $W_{\rm minimal}$ we show they have, respectively, dimensions $1$, $15$, and $29$, and prove that each of the $M_i$ is a rational variety, while for $W_{\rm MSSM}$ we show that $M_3$ is the only component. Restricting the $M_i$ to the electroweak sector, we recover known results. We describe the components of the vacuum moduli space geometrically in terms of incidence varieties to a product of Segre varieties.

</details>


### [211] [Decorating Asymptotically Flat Space-Time with the Moduli Space of String Theory](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.13876)
*Ashoke Sen*

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>

Abstract: N=2, 4 and 8 supersymmetric string theories in four dimensional flat space-time have moduli space of vacua. We argue that starting from a theory where the moduli approach a particular moduli space point A at infinity, we can construct a classical solution that contains an arbitrarily large space-time region where the moduli take values corresponding to any other moduli space point B of our choice to any desired accuracy. Therefore the observables of a theory with a given set of asymptotic values of the moduli will have complete information on the observables for any other asymptotic values of the moduli. Also it is physically impossible for any experiment, performed over a finite time, to determine the asymptotic values of the moduli. We point out the difference between asymptotically flat space-time and asymptotically AdS space-time in this regard and discuss the possible implication of these results for holographic duals of string theories in flat space-time. For N=2 supersymmetric theories, A and B could correspond to compactifications on topologically distinct Calabi-Yau manifolds related by flop or conifold transitions.

### [212] [Probing Non-Graviton Spectra in $\mathcal{N}=4$ SYM via BMN truncation and S-Duality](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.13887)
*Abhijit Gadde,Eunwoo Lee,Rajat Raj,Shivansh Tomar*

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究N=4 SYM的量子对称性和上同调结构，发掘其在不同对偶性和截断条件下的新现象，特别是BMN截断下新玻色子小宇宙的存在。

Method: 该论文系统地使用了留数方法，详细计算了不同SU(N)群的BMN上同调指标，找到闭合表达式并分析了分子和分母中的模式，揭示了新的玻色子谱。

Abstract: The one-loop cohomology of N=4 SYM is conjectured to be isomorphic to the exact cohomology. As a result, its truncations are expected to be subrings of the exact cohomology. We study the superconformal index restricted over one such truncation known as the BMN truncation. We present a systematic algorithm to compute the BMN index using the method of residues. We compute the BMN index for SU(N) SYM for N = 2,...,6 in closed form. It is expressed as a rational function of the fugacity. A term of the type (1-x) in the denominator indicates the presence of a bosonic generator counted with fugacity x. We find a rich and universal set of such terms in the denominator showing an interesting bosonic Fock space in the spectrum of protected operators. This Fock space cannot be explained as coming from the non-interacting supersymmetric graviton gas far away from the black hole as in the grey-galaxy solutions because the charges of the bosonic generators are not compatible with those of the supersymmetric gravitons. This suggests a novel microstructure within the supersymmetric black hole itself. We also examine the indices of S-dual pairs SO(2N+1) and Sp(N) SYM. Although their full 1/16-BPS indices coincide, we find discrepancies in their BMN-sector indices. As the BMN indices restricted to the graviton sector are expected to be the same, this mismatch allows us to identify non-graviton cohomologies. We explicitly find one of them in the SO(7) theory that is responsible for the mismatch of the BMN index. We also show that indices restricted to other one-loop cohomology truncations, in general, do not match under S-duality. If the conjecture of exactness of one-loop cohomology is correct, this suggests the presence of new cohomology subrings that match under S-duality with the letter-based truncations of the one-loop cohomology. This offers a way to check the one-loop exactness conjecture.

*Jefferson Monção da Silva,João Paulo M. Pitelli*

  <summary>Details</summary>

Abstract: The quantum detection of spacetime conicity was investigated in reference [Phys. Lett. B 820, 136482 (2021)] through the analysis of the response function of an Unruh-deWitt detector coupled to a massless scalar field. In particular, it was shown that the detector can discern the presence of the deficit angle of a region of spacetime even when it is placed on a flat region with no conical deficit and (due to the rapid switching on and off) is classically isolated from the conical region. In this paper, we study the response function of the Unruh-deWitt detector on the same classical framework, but exploring the effects of the choice of boundary conditions for the scalar field at the connecting hypersurface. These boundary conditions are extracted from the two-interval Sturm-Liouville theory and each one gives rise to a physically inequivalent sensible dynamics for the quantum field. We show that they play an important role on the response function of the detector, which effectively ``feels'' the combined effect of conicity + boundary condition.

  <summary>Details</summary>

Result: Massive scalar particles exhibit non-local propagation on chiral higher-spin backgrounds, similar to massless cases.

Abstract: Previously, we showed that massless scalar point particles cannot propagate on classical backgrounds of chiral higher-spin theory. This conclusion was derived from the analysis of the light-cone consistency conditions occurring at the second order in interactions. In the present paper, we extend this result to the case of massive particles, showing that these cannot propagate on chiral higher-spin backgrounds either. In order to do that, we use a different and more direct approach, which does not rely on special simplifications occurring for massless particles. Namely, we solve the light-cone consistency conditions at the given order in complete generality and then show that all the Hamiltonians found are inevitably non-local. We emphasise connections between the resulting procedure and the on-shell methods applied to worldline scattering observables.

TL;DR: The paper presents a study of a 5-point Liouville conformal block with a level 2 degenerate field insertion. The solution is conjectured to be a hypergeometric function and its derivative, with simplified recursion relations. <details>
  <summary>Details</summary>

Conclusion: This work, by proving the conjecture and connecting regions through hypergeometric functions, contributes foundational tools for conformal field theories and their applications in black hole perturbation theory.

Abstract: In this paper we investigate 5-point Liouville conformal block with a level 2 degenerate field insertion. Our main tool is the BPZ differential equation, which, upon placing three of the insertions at the standard positions $\infty$, $1$, and $0$, reduces to a linear differential equation which is of order two in the degenerate insertion point $z$, and order one in the remaining point $x$. In a previous paper, it was conjectured that the solution could be expressed in terms of a single hypergeometric function and its derivative, with coefficients computable via recursive relations up to the desired order $x^k$. In this paper, we simplify these recursion relations and provide a rigorous inductive proof of the conjecture.
  Our representation of the 5-point conformal block readily facilitates the connection between various analyticity regions through classical connection formulae for the hypergeometric function.
  In the quasi-classical limit, the 5-point BPZ equation reduces to the Heun equation. Consequently, we recover a recently proposed representation of the Heun equation in terms of a single hypergeometric function, which has proven to be highly effective in the analysis of gravitational perturbation of black holes.

This corresponds to the leading term (0SF) in the gravitational self-force expansion for the spinning two-body problem with large mass hierarchy. ### [220] [Structure of the $\mathcal{N}=4$ chiral algebra](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14655)
*Matthias R. Gaberdiel,Wei Li*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: 研究显示，4D N=4 SU(N)超杨米尔斯理论的 chirality 代数是一个 N=4 超共形顶点算子代数。通过分析乘积展开的结合性，发现该代数由唯一的中心电荷参数定义，而没有额外的自由参数。此外，OPE 系数的截断模式表明该代数不能来源于对称分形。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究超杨米尔斯理论和相关的数学结构，有助于更深入理解该理论在更高维度或不同背景下的行为，以及相关的超对称性质。

Method: 使用递归方法分析乘积展开的结合性，推导出代数的结构参数，发现只有中心电荷参数影响。

Result: 该研究证明该 chirality 代数由中心电荷唯一确定，且其结构不同于对称分形。这意味着该代数可能来自不同的数学构造，而不仅仅是对称分形。

Conclusion: 结果揭示了 4D N=4 SU(N) 理论 chirality 代数的唯一性和其非对称分形来源，进一步丰富了我们对这些代数结构的理解，可能促进新理论的开发或应用。

Abstract: The chiral algebra of 4D $\mathcal{N}=4$ SU$(N)$ super-Yang-Mills theory is an $\mathcal{N}=4$ superconformal vertex operator algebra. We analyse the structure of this algebra by studying recursively the constraints that are required by the associativity of the operator product expansion. We find that the algebra is uniquely characterized by the central charge (which can take an arbitrary value), without any additional free parameter. Furthermore, the truncation pattern of the OPE coefficients suggests that the algebra cannot arise from the symmetric orbifold.

</details>


### [221] [Higher loops in AdS: applications to boundary CFT](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14699)

  <summary>Details</summary>

Abstract: The Euclidean Anti-de Sitter (AdS) space provides a natural framework for studying boundary conformal field theory (BCFT). <details>
  <summary>Details</summary>

Abstract: We construct Abelian gauge field configurations that carry non-zero instanton
number. Each such "Abelian instanton" is generated by a closed magnetic
worldline in four-dimensional Euclidean space, provided the Abelian gauge field
has non-trivial winding along the closed worldline. The resulting field
configuration corresponds to a Euclidean dyon loop featuring non-zero instanton
number. We embed these dyon loops in a UV-complete theory using the
Georgi-Glashow model and show that the full instanton charge is borne entirely

Abstract: We calculate the $\theta$ dependence in a cousin of QCD, where the vacuum
structure can be analyzed exactly. The theory is $\mathcal{N}=2$ $SU(2)$ gauge
theory with $N_F=0,1,2,3$ flavors of fundamentals, explicitly broken to

supersymmetry breaking (AMSB). The hierarchy $m_{AMSB}\ll
\mu_{\mathcal{N}=1}\ll \Lambda$ ensures the validity of our IR analysis. As

### [225] [Can weak-gravity, causality-violation arguments constrain modified gravity?](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14889)
*Stephon Alexander,Heliudson Bernardo,Nicolás Yunes*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: The paper discusses the limitations of causality arguments derived from flat-spacetime amplitudes based on the eikonal limit of gravitational scattering, particularly focusing on their applicability to modified gravity theories. The study shows that these constraints are less stringent compared to astrophysical bounds and are significantly weaker even in transplanckian scattering. Special emphasis is placed on dynamical Chern-Simons gravity, though conclusions are relevant to other modified gravity theories as well. The paper also explores how time delays can be derived from various solutions, such as black holes, neutron stars, and shockwaves, and finds that time delays are suppressed in certain regimes. Additionally, the impact of graviton nonlinearities in strong gravity regions is briefly discussed. Overall, the findings suggest that amplitude-based causality constraints are generally not as strict as other experimental and observational bounds.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Understanding the limitations of causality as a tool in probing modified gravity is important for narrowing down viable theories that could explain observed phenomena without contradicting known physical principles. This paper contributes to that understanding by examining the specific scenarios where such constraints might be applicable and the relative strengths of different experimental bounds.

Method: The authors analyze the eikonal limit of gravitational scattering, calculate the relevant amplitudes in different modified gravity models, and derive expressions for causality constraints. They compare these constraints with astrophysical observations, such as those from gravitational waves from black hole mergers, to determine their applicability and strength in constraining modified gravity theories.

Result: The paper demonstrates that causality-based constraints from flat spacetime amplitudes are only applicable in the weak-gravity regime and are not stringent compared to other experimental and observational bounds, particularly for transplanckian scattering. Dynamical Chern-Simons gravity is shown to be less constrained by these arguments. Time delay calculations also reveal suppression factors dependent on object mass and impact parameter, and positive results within the validity of shockwave solutions further support the applicability limitations.

Conclusion: Amplitude-based causality arguments are generally not a strong constraint on modified gravity theories. Other observational and experimental methods, such as astrophysical observations of gravitational waves and other phenomena, provide stricter bounds. These findings rely on dynamical Chern-Simons gravity but suggest that similar conclusions likely apply to other modified gravity models as well.

Abstract: We investigate limitations of causality arguments from flat-spacetime
amplitudes, based on the eikonal limit of gravitational scattering, to place
constraints on modified gravity. We show that causality constraints are only
valid in the weak-gravity regime even for transplanckian scattering, and that
such constraints are much less stringent than astrophysical ones, obtained for
example from gravitational waves emitted in black hole coalescence. Special
attention is given to the weakness of causality constraints on dynamical
Chern-Simons gravity, but our results apply to other modified gravity theories
as well. In the context of that theory, we also discuss how to obtain a
time-delay formula from black hole, neutron stars, and shockwave solutions. For
scattering with compact objects, we explicitly show that time delays are
greatly suppressed by the ratio of the object's mass to the impact parameter,
so time advances only occur greatly outside the cut off of the theory. For the
shockwave solution, we find that the time delay is always positive within the
regime of validity of the solution. We also comment on the impact of graviton
nonlinearities for time-delay calculations in the nonlinear, strong gravity
regime. We conclude that amplitude-based causality constraints on modified
gravity are typically not stringent relative to other experimental and
observational bounds.

### [226] [Worldsheet CFT$_2$ and Celestial CFT$_2$ : An AdS$_3$-CFT$_2$ perspective](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14891)
*Shamik Banerjee,Nishant Gupta,Sagnik Misra*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: This paper connects celestial conformal field theories (CFTs) with gravitational theories in higher dimensions, suggesting that near-boundary scaling limits of certain gravity theories can dual to celestial CFTs with reduced symmetries. The paper proposes that such dualities arise due to contracted conformal groups when approaching the boundary of anti-de Sitter (AdS) space. An example is given with bosonic string theory on Euclidean AdS_3, where the near-boundary limit describes a long string wrapping the AdS boundary and is dual to a Liouville CFT. The conclusion highlights that while this approach yields a Celestial CFT_2 with only Lorentz symmetry, it does not fully yield an ISO(3,1) invariant CFT_2 because the gravitational theory lacks conformal invariance.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper seems to be exploring deep connections between quantum gravity and conformal field theories, possibly through the holographic principle. The idea of celestial CFTs suggests a new framework for understanding the boundary description of gravitational theories in asymptotically flat spacetimes.

Method: The paper begins by introducing the concept of celestial CFT_d and relates it to the AdS/CFT correspondence. It argues that by taking the near-boundary limit in EAdS_{d+1}, one can obtain a CFT_d whose symmetry group matches the contracted conformal group. The method involves analyzing the scaling behavior of gravitational theories under this limit and identifying the resulting dual CFT structure. Specific examples with AdS_3 and bosonic string theory are used to illustrate the concepts, demonstrating how the near-boundary limit leads to recognizable dual theories like Liouville CFT.

Result: The main result is that celestial CFTs with reduced symmetry groups can be constructed as duals to gravitational theories near their boundaries. Specifically, taking the near-boundary limit of conformal gravity on EAdS_{d+1} leads to a CFT_d with ISO(d+1,1) symmetry, forming a Celestial CFT_d. Similarly, non-conformal gravity theories lead to CFTs with only Lorentz invariance. In the case of string theory on AdS_3, the dual CFT_2 is a Liouville theory, an example of a Celestial CFT_2 with only SO(3,1) symmetry. The paper concludes that without conformal invariance in the bulk, a conventional ISO(3,1) CFT_2 on the celestial sphere might not be fully recovered.

Conclusion: The paper contributes to understanding how celestial conformal field theories emerge as duals to gravitational theories in higher asymptotically flat spacetimes. By examining specific cases like AdS_3 and bosonic string theory, it illustrates the mechanisms through which the bulk gravitational theory's near-boundary limit translates to a dual CFT, demonstrating both the success and limitations of this approach depending on the presence or absence of conformal symmetry in the bulk theory. It suggests that celestial CFTs provide a promising avenue for exploring quantum gravity in the asymptotically flat regime without relying on the AdS/CFT correspondence, highlighting their unique features and potential applications in understanding gravitational phenomena in flat space.

Abstract: Celestial CFT$_d$ is the putative dual of quantum gravity in asymptotically
flat $(d+2)$ dimensional space time. We argue that a class of Celestial CFT$_d$
can be engineered via AdS$_{d+1}$-CFT$_d$ correspondence. Our argument is based
on the observation that if we zoom in near the boundary of (Euclidean)
AdS$_{d+1}$ then the conformal isometry group of EAdS$_{d+1}$, which is
SO$(d+2,1)$, contracts to the Poincare group ISO$(d+1,1)$. This suggests that
the near boundary scaling limit of a theory of \textit{conformal} gravity on
EAdS$_{d+1}$ should be dual to a boundary CFT$_d$ with ISO$(d+1,1)$ symmetry.
This dual CFT$_d$, since the symmetries match, is an example of a Celestial
CFT$_d$. Similarly, if we have a \textit{non-conformal} theory of gravity on
EAdS$_{d+1}$ then the near boundary scaling limit of such a theory is dual to a
(boundary) Celestial CFT$_d$ with \textit{only} (SO$(d+1,1)$) Lorentz
invariance. Celestial CFTs with only Lorentz invariance have been recently
studied in the literature. Now following this logic we discuss, among other
things, the near boundary scaling limit of the bosonic string theory on
Euclidean AdS$_3$ in the presence of the NS-NS B field. The AdS$_3$ part of the
worldsheet theory is free in this limit and has been studied in the literature
in different contexts. This limit describes a ``long string'' which wraps the
(Euclidean) AdS$_3$ boundary and it has been argued that the space-time CFT$_2$
which describes the radial fluctuations of a long string is a Liouville CFT.
According to our proposal, the dual CFT$_2$ which describes the \textit{long
string sector} is an example of a \textit{Celestial} CFT$_2$ with \textit{only}
(SO$(3,1)$)Lorentz invariance. We do not get a full ISO$(3,1)$ invariant
Celestial CFT$_2$ in this way because the string theory does not have target
space conformal invariance.

</details>

Abstract: We introduce a simple model to realize the free real scalar CFT on the fuzzy

a single tuning parameter-the conformal coupling. We numerically demonstrate
that our model correctly reproduces the operator spectrum, correlation
functions, and, crucially, the harmonic oscillator algebra of the real scalar
CFT. We also examine the fuzzy sphere algebra, a generalization of the
Girvin-MacDonald-Platzman algebra, and discuss its potential implications for
defining quantum field theories on non-commutative geometries. Finally, we
propose wavefunction ansatz for the ground states of both the free scalar and
Ising CFTs, which exhibit remarkable agreement with the CFT ground state
wavefunctions of the fuzzy sphere model. For instance, the wavefunction overlap
between our Ising ansatz and the Ising CFT ground state exceeds $0.99$ for
$N=28$ fermions, suggesting a promising direction for tackling the 3D Ising
CFT.

### [231] [Classical analog of the T. D. Lee model for renormalization](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15161)
*K. Xu,C. P. Sun*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: The paper presents a classical counterpart to the Lee model in quantum field theory, showing that mass divergence and renormalization procedures are not exclusively quantum features. It compares classical and quantum phenomena, challenging the quantum-centric view and providing insights into classical-quantum correspondence.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: This paper aims to explore whether classical systems can exhibit phenomena similar to those in quantum field theory, particularly mass divergence and renormalization.

Method: The authors analyze a classical model of coupled harmonic oscillators (CHO) and compare its behavior to the quantum Lee model. They examine frequency divergence, renormalization procedures, and scattering processes in both systems to establish parallels.

Result: The study demonstrates that classical coupled oscillators exhibit frequency divergence and mass renormalization, similar to quantum mass divergence. It also shows that classical and quantum scattering processes mirror each other, challenging the quantum-centric perspective on renormalization.

Conclusion: This work broadens the understanding of renormalization beyond quantum mechanics, suggesting classical systems can exhibit similar phenomena and implying deeper connections between classical and quantum theories in renormalization.

Abstract: While divergence and renormalization of physical quantities are frequently
encountered in quantum field theory (QFT), they are not necessarily
quantum-specific characteristics. We show in this paper that there exists a
classical counterpart of the Lee model which is the model of coupled harmonic
oscillators (CHO). It is demonstrated that the frequency divergence in this
classical model precisely replicates the phenomenon of mass divergence in the
Lee model, as does the corresponding renormalization procedure. Considering the
arbitrariness in renormalization schemes, we establish necessary conditions
that a general renormalization must satisfy for the model of two coupled
oscillators which corresponds to the single-mode Lee model. Furthermore, we
analyze the classical analog of $N\text{-}\theta$ scattering process and show
that the dependence of scattering strength on the cutoff mode mirrors that of
the quantum case. These findings challenge the quantum-centric view of mass
renormalization in the Lee model and offer new insights into the
classical-quantum correspondence in renormalization theories.

</details>

Abstract: Exploring quantum effects from black hole thermodynamics has always been a
pivotal topic. In recent years, the free energy landscape and ensemble-averaged

quantities consistent with the effective action define a valid thermodynamics.
Furthermore, the phase diagram was modified by the off-shell effects, resulting
in a more abundant phase structure. We discover that the traditional black hole
thermodynamics can be recovered in the semi-classical limit. The region of
first-order phase transitions shrinks and zero-order phase transitions emerge
when off-shell effects are included. The results provide new perspectives for
understanding the quantum corrections in black hole thermodynamics.

### [234] [Exact results on the Bethe Ansatz evaluation of the SCI](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15296)
*Antonio Amariti,Pietro Glorioso*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: The paper compares the Bethe Ansatz approach with direct evaluation for computing indices in certain gauge theories. The BA approach sometimes doesn't match the direct results, especially for large SU(N), but exactness holds for some examples.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The authors wanted to validate the Bethe Ansatz method against direct computations for superconformal indices, which are important in understanding gauge theories.

Method: Used Bethe Ansatz (BA) approach on SU(2) and SU(N) gauge groups, compared results with direct evaluations.

Result: BA results didn't match direct evaluations for SU(2) and SU(N≥3); needed continuous solutions for SU(N) but matched exactly for T^{1,1} and partly for the suspended pinch point without continuous contributions.

Conclusion: Bethe Ansatz has limitations but accurately computes indices for T^{1,1} and similar manifolds when continuous solutions are excluded.

Abstract: We evaluate the superconformal index using the Bethe Ansatz (BA) approach for
4d $\mathcal{N}=1$ toric quiver gauge theories with a small amount of gauge
groups. We restrict to $\mathrm{SU}(2)$ gauge factors and compare the results
with the ones obtained by a direct evaluation of the index. The answer obtained
from the BA approach using only discrete solutions for the BA equations does
not always reproduce the direct evaluation result. A similar problem affects
the case of $\mathrm{SU}(N)$ $\mathcal{N}=4$ SYM for $N \geq 3$, and it
requires to introduce continuous solutions to the BA equations. However, we
find that for $T^{1,1}$ and partially for the suspended pinch point the
matching is exact in absence of the contributions from continuous solutions.

### [235] [All zeros of (super)String Theory](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15299)
*Yu-Chi Chang,Hsing-Yen Chen,Yu-tin Huang*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: The paper explores the zeros of string theory using curve-integral representation, examining bosonic and super-tachyon amplitudes, and discusses implications for super-Yang-Mills theory.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To understand the mathematical structure and zeros of string theory, particularly focusing on tachyon and super-tachyon amplitudes and their implications for super-Yang-Mills theory.

Method: The authors use curve-integral representation and OPE limits to analyze scattering amplitudes for different string theories, deriving the zeros from these amplitudes.

Result: The paper identifies shared zeros between tachyon and scaffolded amplitudes and introduces new zeros from super-tachyon amplitudes, suggesting potential connections to supersymmetry and super-Yang-Mills theory. Four and six-point gluino amplitudes are analyzed, contributing to the recovery of super-Yang-Mills via scaffolding. Field theory limits of fermionic amplitudes are considered.

Conclusion: The study provides new insights into string theory zeros and their relation to supersymmetry and super-Yang-Mills theory, offering a framework that recovers these field theories through scaffolded amplitudes. This contributes to the understanding of string theory's mathematical underpinnings and its connections to gauge theories.

Abstract: In this paper, we study the zeros of string theory utilizing its
curve-integral representation. Firstly, we note that for bosonic strings the
tachyon amplitude in curve-representation is identical to the kinematic shifted
Tr$\phi^3$ amplitude. Scaffolding is then equivalent to taking the OPE limit of
vertex operators on the string world-sheet, which yields amplitude of higher
excitations. Using this picture, we derive that the $n$-point level-$N$
scattering amplitude shares the same set of zeros as the $n$-point tachyon
amplitude as well as those inherited from it's prescaffold image, i.e.
$(2^N)n$-point. Doing the same for the super-tachyon amplitude, exposes new
zeros for the open super-string, which can be viewed as the avatar of
supersymmetry. Finally we also consider the gluino amplitude at four and
six-points, identifying its zero and recovering super-Yang-Mills via
scaffolding. Finally we consider the field theory limit of colored fermion
amplitudes from the curve-integral form.

*Carmelo P. Martin*

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究非交换时空下的粒子散射过程中的纠缠生成，可能揭示时空结构与量子纠缠之间的联系。

Method: 使用旋度为零的非交换时空模型，研究树级散射过程。计算了两种光子和两种费米子的散射过程的夹杂度。通过计算散射角度和非交换参数θ矩阵，找出导致最大纠缠的条件。

Result: 在正交碰撞时，夹杂度随能量、θ矩阵及其入射角度变化；当θ=π/2时，存在某些角度下不产生纠缠。
