### [316] [Multilevel Electromagnetically Induced Transparency Cooling](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14546)
*Katya Fouka,Athreya Shankar,Ting Rei Tan,Arghavan Safavi-Naini*

Main category: physics.atom-ph

TL;DR: 研究扩展了EIT冷却到多能级系统，增加了至少一个暗态，提供了冷却速率的估算。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 文章扩展了EIT冷却到多能级系统，提供了新的方法来提高冷却效率，这是对 trapped ion量子信息处理的关键贡献。

Method: 论文开发了一个用于多能级系统冷却的正式分析方法，特别是弱次声耦合和强次声耦合的速率估算。

Result: 扩展后的EIT冷却方法在多能级系统中实现了更快的冷却，这得益于引入的暗态和新的冷却速率估计。

Conclusion: 该方法为trapped ion系统的量子计算提供了更有效的冷却途径，有助于提升数据处理能力。

Abstract: Electromagnetically Induced Transparency (EIT) cooling is a well-established method for preparing trapped ion systems in their motional ground state. However, isolating a three-level system, as required for EIT cooling, is often challenging or impractical. In this work, we extend the EIT cooling framework to multilevel systems where the number of ground states exceeds the number of excited states, ensuring the presence of at least one dark state. We develop a formalism to accurately determine the cooling rate in the weak sideband coupling regime and provide an approximate estimate for cooling rates beyond this regime, without the need for explicit simulation of the motional degree of freedom. We clarify the connection between the cooling rate and the absorption spectrum, offering a pathway for efficient near-ground-state cooling of ions with complex electronic structures.

</details>


### [317] [High-fidelity quantum state control of a polar molecular ion in a cryogenic environment](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14740)
*Dalton Chaffee,Baruch Margulis,April Sheffield,Julian Schmidt,April Reisenfeld,David R. Leibrandt,Dietrich Leibfried,Chin-Wen Chou*

Main category: physics.atom-ph

TL;DR: The paper presents an innovative method for controlling and measuring the quantum state of a CaH+ ion using a quantum-logic spectroscopy (QLS) protocol. By employing a Bayesian update scheme and repeated adaptive probes in a cryogenic environment, they achieve high state preparation and measurement fidelity with significant improvements in coherence times and measurement contrast.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: This research is significant as it advances quantum control and spectroscopy techniques, which are fundamental for quantum information processing and precision metrology.

Method: The researchers employ a quantum-logic spectroscopy (QLS) protocol, using repeated adaptive probes and a Bayesian update scheme in a cryogenic setup to achieve reduced thermal radiation effects. Their method involves detecting outcomes using an atomic ion and updating confidence levels to quantify molecular state information.

Result: They demonstrate state preparation and measurement (SPAM) in a single quantum state with a fidelity of under 6×10⁻³ and measure Rabi flopping with over 99% contrast. The protocol avoids molecular-specific lasers and uses a non-destructive detection scheme, showing advancements in quantum state manipulation and measurement precision.

Conclusion: This work sets a new benchmark for SPAM fidelity in single molecular quantum states and contributes to the development of quantum technologies like quantum computing and metrology.

Abstract: We use a quantum-logic spectroscopy (QLS) protocol to control the quantum state of a CaH+ ion in a cryogenic environment, in which reduced thermal radiation extends rotational state lifetimes by an order of magnitude over those at room temperature. By repeatedly and adaptively probing the molecule, detecting the outcome of each probe via an atomic ion, and using a Bayesian update scheme to quantify confidence in the molecular state, we demonstrate state preparation and measurement (SPAM) in a single quantum state with infidelity less than $6\times10^{-3}$ and measure Rabi flopping between two states with greater than 99% contrast. The protocol does not require any molecule-specific lasers and the detection scheme is non-destructive. To our knowledge, this result represents the highest SPAM fidelity of a single molecular quantum state demonstrated to date.

</details>

We clarify the connection between the cooling rate and the absorption spectrum, offering a pathway for efficient near-ground-state cooling of ions with complex electronic structures.

### [320] [High-fidelity quantum state control of a polar molecular ion in a cryogenic environment](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14740)
*Dalton Chaffee,Baruch Margulis,April Sheffield,Julian Schmidt,April Reisenfeld,David R. Leibrandt,Dietrich Leibfried,Chin-Wen Chou*

Main category: physics.atom-ph

TL;DR: 该研究利用量子逻辑光谱学协议控制钙离子的状态，并在 cryogenic 环境中延长分子旋转态寿命，显著提高了态的准备与测量信度和Rabi 跳跃对比度，具有目前最高单分子量子态的态态之间信度。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 该研究展示了通过不依赖分子特定激光器的协议，在 cryogenic 环境中高效地实现单分子量子态的态态信息获取，这在量子计算和量子通信有潜在的应用。

Method: 使用量子逻辑光谱学协议，通过重复和自适应的探测，利用贝叶斯更新方案来提高信度。

Result: 成功实现了态准备和测量，并在进行了贝叶斯更新后，达到了 6e-3 的信度和 99% 的Rabi 跳跃对比度。

Conclusion: 该研究的方法在单分子量子态的信度和对比度上达到了目前最高水平，具有理论和技术应用的意义。

Abstract: We use a quantum-logic spectroscopy (QLS) protocol to control the quantum state of a CaH+ ion in a cryogenic environment, in which reduced thermal radiation extends rotational state lifetimes by an order of magnitude over those at room temperature. By repeatedly and adaptively probing the molecule, detecting the outcome of each probe via an atomic ion, and using a Bayesian update scheme to quantify confidence in the molecular state, we demonstrate state preparation and measurement (SPAM) in a single quantum state with infidelity less than $6\times10^{-3}$ and measure Rabi flopping between two states with greater than 99% contrast. The protocol does not require any molecule-specific lasers and the detection scheme is non-destructive. To our knowledge, this result represents the highest SPAM fidelity of a single molecular quantum state demonstrated to date.

### [321] [Effect of surface magnetism on the x-ray spectra of hollow atoms](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15003)
*P. Dergham,C. Prigent,Ch. V. Ahmad A. Brassart,L. Duval,E. Lamour,S. Macé,S. Steydli,E. M. Tosi,D. Vernhet,M. Trassinelli*

Main category: physics.atom-ph

TL;DR: The study demonstrates that surface magnetism can be detected without an external magnetic field by observing x-ray emission from highly charged ions interacting with a sample. They used Ar¹⁷+ ion emission to track the ionization state during a phase transition, concluding that ferro-paramagnetic phase transition occurs when the ion shell fills. This resolves disputes from earlier studies.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper addresses a long-standing debate in materials science regarding the detection of surface magnetism without an external field. Using ion emission spectroscopy, it provides new evidence about the ferro-paramagnetic phase transition.

Method: The method involves using Ar¹⁷+ ions at grazing incidence to detect x-ray emissions, specifically measuring the 3 keV transition. Temperature variation is used to observe changes in the ion's shell state.

Result: The ion population evolves from half-filled to full shell, indicating magnetic ordering occurs when the shell is filled. This method confirms surface magnetism detection without external fields.

Conclusion: The study conclusively shows that magnetism at the surface can be detected without an external field, resolving previous contradictions in ion-surface interaction studies.

Abstract: We present evidence that the detection of surface magnetism without the
application of an external magnetic field is possible by studying the x-ray
emission of highly charged ions interacting at grazing incidence with the
sample. Measuring the 3 keV $n=2 \to 1$ transition in the interaction of
Ar\textsuperscript{17+} with a nickel sample at various temperatures gives
access to the $n=2$ ion population. The latter evolves from a half-filled to a
full shell during the ferro-paramagnetic phase transition of the sample, with
the ferromagnetic phase reflecting the filling blocking due to Pauli principle.
This finding puts an end to a longstanding controversy arising from
contradictory studies of ion--surface interaction using Auger spectroscopy.

</details>


### [322] [Response of Comagnetometer to Exotic Spin-Dependent Couplings](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15046)

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper explores the application and improvement of comagnetometers in measuring exotic spin-dependent interactions, particularly in dark matter research. The authors derive formulas and propose a new calibration method, which is crucial for advancing dark matter detection.

Method: The authors conducted theoretical and experimental studies on the frequency response of a differential comagnetometer. They derived analytical expressions for the frequency response to magnetic fields and exotic couplings, established a conversion relationship between them, and developed a light-shift-based calibration protocol.

Result:  they show improved method for determining axion coupling strengths and propose a new calibration protocol. Therefore, comagnetometers can be enhanced for detecting exotic fields and dark matter.

Conclusion: Enhancing comagnetometers' capabilities for detecting exotic spin-dependent interactions like dark matter is achieved through theoretical analysis and experimental validation, with a revised method and new calibration protocol to improve sensitivity and accuracy.

Abstract: Comagnetometers offer unique advantages in measuring exotic spin-dependent
interactions by suppressing magnetic noise. Understanding the frequency
response to exotic interactions is essential for evaluating and improving the
sensitivity of comagnetometers, as the signals often exhibit distinct spectral
features. We conduct theoretical and experimental studies on the frequency
response of a differential comagnetometer. We derive analytical expressions for
the frequency response of the differential comagnetometer to both magnetic
field and exotic couplings, along with the conversion relationship between
them. Based on this, we revise the method for determining the axion-nucleon
coupling strength with comagnetometers. Furthermore, we introduce a
light-shift-based calibration protocol to verify the response to exotic
interactions. This work helps predict the sensitivity of comagnetometers in
detecting exotic fields and advances the exploration of dark matter.

### [323] [Compatibility of trapped ions and dielectrics at cryogenic temperatures](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15057)
*M. Bruff,L. Sonderhouse,K. N. David,J. Stuart,D. H. Slichter,D. Leibfried*

Main category: physics.atom-ph

TL;DR: The paper investigates the impact of unshielded dielectric materials on ion traps near optical fibers, showing measurable electric fields and ion heating. They can be compensated, and using such dielectrics in traps is viable.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The exploration of dielectric effects in ion trapping could enhance trap design and improve sensitivity, especially in cryogenic environments used for precision measurements like absolute IAS or cold atoms.

Method: The authors trap a 40Ca+ ion near an optical fiber, measure electric fields and ion thermal motion, and assess the feasibility of integrating dielectric objects into traps.

Result: Measured up to ~30 quantum motions and ~1.5 MHz motional frequency, with electric fields up to a few kV/m that are compensable.

Conclusion: Using integrated dielectric elements could improve trap efficiency and design without sacrificing performance, supporting applications in precision metrology and research on fundamental physics.

Abstract: We study the impact of an unshielded dielectric $\unicode{x2013}$ here, a
bare optical fiber $\unicode{x2013}$ on a $^{40}$Ca${^+}$ ion held several
hundred $\mu$m away in a cryogenic surface electrode trap. We observe
distance-dependent stray electric fields of up to a few kV/m due to the
dielectric, which drift on average less than 10% per month and can be fully
compensated with reasonable voltages on the trap electrodes. We observe ion
motional heating rates attributable to the dielectric of $\approx$30 quanta per
second at an ion-fiber distance of 215(4) $\mu$m and $\approx$1.5 MHz motional
frequency. These results demonstrate the viability of using unshielded,
trap-integrated dielectric objects such as miniature optical cavities or other
optical elements in cryogenic surface electrode ion traps.

</details>


### [324] [Selective Bond Breaking in CO$_2^{2+}$ Induced by Photoelectron Recoil](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15177)
*J. Weiherer,N. Melzer,M. Kircher,A. Pier,L. Kaiser,J. Kruse,N. Anders,J. Stindl,L. Sommerlad,O. D. McGinnis,M. Schmidt,J. Drnec,F. Trinter,M. S. Schöffler,L. Ph. H. Schmidt,N. Sisourat,S. Eckart,T. Jahnke,R. Dörner*

Main category: physics.atom-ph

TL;DR: The paper shows that CO₂ ionization through core-ionization leads to Auger-Meitner decay, with bond cleavage influenced by photoelectron direction, causing a significant dipole effect. The main finding is that O⁺ is emitted opposite to the light's direction. The experiment has strong implications for understanding CO₂ ion behavior in ion thrusters. The methodology involved classical trajectory Monte Carlo simulations and experiments with laser and ion detection. The results suggest potential applications for controlling O⁺ emission, though further testing is needed.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Understanding CO₂ ionization and bond cleavage is crucial for applications in space exploration, such as ion.thrusters, where controlling charged species is essential. The asymmetric emission could be leveraged to optimize performance or avoid harmful emissions.

Method: The research employs experimental setups using synchrotron radiation, photoelectron detection, and ion momentum analysis along with Monte Carlo simulations to model the process and predict emission angles.

Result: The key result is the observed 25% asymmetry in bond cleavage, leading to O⁺ being emitted opposite to light propagation, which creates a significant dipole effect in molecular dissociation. This effect is significant for understanding and controlling CO₂ ion behavior.

Conclusion: The study concludes that the directionality of photoelectron recoil influences how CO₂ ions dissociate, resulting in a dipole effect that impacts the emission of O⁺. This has implications for optimizing molecular thrusters and could lead to advancements in space-related technologies by better controlling charged species behavior.

Abstract: After core-ionization of CO$_2$, typically an Auger-Meitner decay takes
place, leading to the formation of a dicationic molecule that may dissociate
into CO$^+$ and O$^+$. We demonstrate experimentally that the recoil momentum
of the photoelectron steers, which of the two equivalent bonds breaks during
the dissociation. At 20 keV photon energy, we observe an asymmetry of up to 25%
for bond cleavage that depends on the emission direction of the photoelectron.
Furthermore, we show that this effect leads to a significant nondipole effect
in molecular dissociation in the laboratory frame: O$^+$ fragments are more
likely to be emitted in the direction opposite to the light propagation than
along it.

</details>

### [325] [Numerical investigations of heavy ion driven plasma wakefield acceleration](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14132)
*Jiangdong Li,Jiancheng Yang,Guoxing Xia,Jie Liu,Wenlong Zhan,Ruihu Zhu*

Main category: physics.acc-ph

TL;DR: PBA using heavy ion beams shows potential for high-amplitude wakefields and good energy gain.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper explores a new direction in PBA, heavy-ion beams, to overcome challenges in traditional PBA methods.

Method: Simulations using High Intensity Heavy-ion Accelerator Facility (HIAF) high-energy heavy ion beams generated stable, high-amplitude plasma wakefields up to 6 GV/m.

Result: Results show good performance and suitability for electron acceleration with a potential energy gain of up to 600 TeV per particle.

Conclusion: Heavy-ion beam drivers can be a viable alternative to traditional methods in plasma-based acceleration, offering high efficiency and scalability.

Abstract: Plasma-Based Acceleration (PBA) has emerged as a promising approach to achieve ultra-high gradient particle acceleration. While extensive PBA studies have been conducted using laser, electron, and proton drivers, significant challenges remain in achieving high efficiency, stable acceleration, and scalable energy gain. Meanwhile, due to their higher beam charge density, heavier particle mass and higher kinetic energy, heavy-ion beam drivers represent an interesting direction in PBA research. In this paper, the plasma wakefield acceleration driven by heavy ion beam is studied for the first time, aiming to find the best mechanism for generating high-amplitude wakefields. Using the high intensity, high energy heavy ion beams provided by the High Intensity heavy-ion Accelerator Facility (HIAF), our simulations show that heavy ions can excite stable, high-amplitude plasma wakefields up to 6 GV/m, suitable for electron acceleration. These results show good performance of heavy ion beam drivers and their potential as a viable and promising approach in the field of PBA.

</details>

### [327] [$μ$LHC: Antimuon Ring and HL-LHC based $μ^+p$ Collider](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15445)
*D. Akturk,A. C. Canbay,H. Dagistanli,B. Dagli,U. Kaya,B. Ketenoglu,A. Kilic,F. Kocak,A. Ozturk,S. Sultansoy,I. Tapan,F. Zimmermann*

Main category: physics.acc-ph

TL;DR: The paper presents a concept for the HL-LHC based antimuon-proton collider ($oldsymbol{
u}$LHC), which plans to achieve a 5.3 TeV center-of-mass energy, surpassing existing colliders. The design leverages the μTRISTAN concept and ultra-cold μ⁺ beam technology from J-PARC. The collider explores two booster ring options and predicts luminosities exceeding $10^{33} cm^{-2}s^{-1}$. The νLHC aims to expand the kinematic plane, especially in small-x and high-Q² regions, aiding QCD research and Higgs boson studies. It also has potential for BSM physics and includes a detector design concept. Given the maturity of cold μ⁺ technology, the νLCH is considered feasible and beneficial for early realization in high-energy physics.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: This paper builds upon existing cold muon beam technology to propose a new high-energy collider, aiming to push the boundaries of high-energy physics research. The motivation is to enhance collider performance and address critical challenges in particle physics.

Method: The paper describes the conceptual design, performance evaluation, and operational feasibility analysis of the νLHC. It involves leveraging the μTRISTAN concept, modeling the collider's components and physics potential, and evaluating luminosity and kinematic coverage.

Result: The proposed νLHC has the potential to achieve a 5.3 TeV center-of-mass energy, achieve luminosities above $10^{33} cm^{-2}s^{-1}$, and cover a wide kinematic range, particularly in small-x and high-Q² regions. This setup is expected to contribute significantly to QCD studies and Higgs boson physics, as well as explore beyond the Standard Model physics with various muon-related phenomena.

Conclusion: The paper concludes that the νLHC represents a feasible and strategically important project for advancing high-energy physics. Its design and projected performance make it a valuable addition to the global collider landscape, particularly for addressing questions related to QCD, the Higgs boson, and beyond the Standard Model physics.

Abstract: Conceptual design and performance evaluation of HL-LHC based antimuon-proton
collider (${\mu}$LHC) are presented. Leveraging the ${\mu}$TRISTAN concept
based on established J-PARC ultra-cold ${\mu}^{+}$ beam technology, ${\mu}$LHC
will give the opportunity to achieve a 5.3 TeV center-of-mass energy,
significantly surpassing EIC and LHeC. Two booster ring options for ${\mu}^{+}$
acceleration, namely, a ${\mu}$TRISTAN-based and a repurposed LHeC ERL-based
systems, are explored. Achievable luminosities are predicted to exceed $10^{33}
cm^{-2}s^{-1}$. The ${\mu}$LHC offers substantially wider kinematic plane
coverage, particularly in small-x and high-$Q^{2}$ regions, significantly
contributing to QCD basics and Higgs boson properties. Its unique potential for
BSM physics extends to muon-related phenomena like excited muons, color-octet
muons, leptoquarks, and contact interactions. A possible detector concept is
also outlined. Given the maturity of ultra-cold ${\mu}^{+}$ beam technology,
${\mu}$LHC is highly feasible for earlier realization than the muon collider,
positioning it as a critical tool for the future of high energy physics.

</details>

### [328] [All-optical convolution utilizing processing in memory based on a cold atomic ensemble](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14716)
*Ying-Hao Ye,Jia-Qi Jiang,En-Ze Li,Wei Zhang,Da-Chuang Li,Zhi-Han Zhu,Dong-Sheng Ding,Bao-Sen Shi*

Main category: physics.app-ph

TL;DR: 研究利用冷原子 ensemble 在光计算中的存储能力，展示了全光子的卷积实验，提高了图像边缘分辨能力，同时提供了超长的相干存储时间，突显了冷原子技术在所有光子 PIM 系统中的潜力。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 光子计算因其高效的计算能力和低延迟逐渐受到重视，使用冷原子技术来提升光子存储与计算的性能，特别是在卷积运算方面，具有重要的理论和应用价值。

Method: 在计算存储基质中，利用冷原子的光子转移特性，通过相位旋转变换实现光子图像在光子存储中的边缘增强，使用时间相关光子成像记录 retrieve 的图像。

Result: 实验结果表明，该方法在边缘增强和存储寿命方面优于现有技术，该系统为全光子 PIM 体系提供了潜在的技术基础。

Conclusion: 研究展示了冷原子 ensemble 在光子计算中的高性能存储能力，为开发全光子 PIM 系统提供了新的技术思路。

Abstract: Processing in memory (PIM) has received significant attention due to its high efficiency, low latency, and parallelism. In optical computation, coherent memory is a crucial infrastructure for PIM frameworks. This study presents an all-optical convolution experiment conducted within computational storage based on a cold atomic ensemble. By exploiting the light-atom phase transfer facilitated by the electromagnetically induced transparency, we demonstrated spiral phase contrast processing of photon images in memory, resulting in the edge enhancement of retrieved images recorded using time-correlated photon imaging. In particular, adopting state-of-the-art atomic techniques provides a coherent memory lifetime exceeding 320 us for PIM operations. Our results highlight the significant potential of cold atomic ensembles as computational storage for developing all-optical PIM systems.

</details>
